<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century_medicine">21st century medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: 21st century medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antibiotics_and_antibiotic_resistance">Antibiotics and antibiotic resistance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Antibiotics and antibiotic resistance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The discovery of <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">penicillin</a> in the 20th century by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Fleming" title="Alexander Fleming">Alexander Fleming</a> provided a vital line of defence against baterical infections that, without them, often cause patients to suffer prelonged recovery periods and highly increased chances of death. Its discovery and application within medicine allowed previously impossible treatments to take place, including <a href="/wiki/Treatment_of_cancer" title="Treatment of cancer">cancer treatments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplantation" title="Organ transplantation">organ transplants</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_surgery" title="Cardiac surgery">open heart surgery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutchings_2019_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hutchings_2019-217">[216]</a></sup> Throughout the 20th century, though, their overprescribed use to humans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> as well as to animals that need them due to the conditions of <a href="/wiki/Intensive_animal_farming" title="Intensive animal farming">intensive animal farming</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> has led to the development of <a href="/wiki/List_of_antibiotic-resistant_bacteria" title="List of antibiotic-resistant bacteria">antibiotic resistant bacteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutchings_2019_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hutchings_2019-217">[216]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Robotics">Robotics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Robotics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2723" data-file-width="3812" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg/220px-WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg/330px-WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg/440px-WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WBAMC_first_in_DoD_to_use_robot_for_surgery_160426-A-EK666-511.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medical personnel place sterilized covers on the arms of the <a href="/wiki/Da_Vinci_Surgical_System" title="Da Vinci Surgical System">daVinci Xi surgical system</a>, a minimally-invasive robotic surgery system, at the William Beaumont Army Medical Center.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pandemics_2">Pandemics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Pandemics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%96_%D0%B7_%D1%85%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%9D%D0%86%D0%94%C2%BB_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%96_%D0%B7_%D1%85%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%9D%D0%86%D0%94%C2%BB_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%27%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%96_%D0%B7_%D1%85%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%9D%D0%86%D0%94%C2%BB_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Ukrainian monument to the HIV pandemic.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="842" data-file-width="1045" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg/220px-Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg/330px-Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg/440px-Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gupima_Covid-19_mu_Rwanda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>COVID-19 swab testing in Rwanda (2021).</div></div></div>
<p>The early 21st century, facilitated by extensive global connections, international travel, and unprecedented human disruption of ecological systems,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> has been defined by a number of noval as well as continuing global <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemics</a> from the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Past">Past</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Past">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/SARS" title="SARS">SARS</a> 2002 to 2004 <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%932004_SARS_outbreak" title="2002–2004 SARS outbreak">outbreak</a> affected a number of countries around the world and killed hundreds. This outbreak gave rise to a number of lessons learnt from viral infection control, including more effective isolation room protocols to better hand washing techniques for medical staff.<b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup></b> A mutated strain of <a href="/wiki/SARS" title="SARS">SARS</a> would go on to develop into <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>, causing the future COVID-19 pandemic. A significant <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza strain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H1N1" title="Influenza A virus subtype H1N1">H1N1</a>, caused a further <a href="/wiki/2009_swine_flu_pandemic" title="2009 swine flu pandemic">pandemic between 2009 to 2010</a>. Known as swine flu, due to its indirect source from pigs, it went on to infect over 700 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ongoing">Ongoing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Ongoing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The continuing <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Epidemiology of HIV/AIDS">HIV pandemic</a>, starting in 1981, has infected and led to the deaths of millions of people around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> Emerging and improved <a href="/wiki/Pre-exposure_prophylaxis" title="Pre-exposure prophylaxis">pre-exposure prophylaxis</a> (PrEP) and <a href="/wiki/Post-exposure_prophylaxis" title="Post-exposure prophylaxis">post-exposure prophylaxis</a> (PEP) treatments that aim to reduce the spread of the disease have proven effective in limiting the spread of HIV<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> alongside combined use of <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">safe sex</a> methods, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_and_reproductive_health" title="Sexual and reproductive health">sexual health education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Needle_and_syringe_programmes" title="Needle and syringe programmes">needle exchange</a> programmes, and sexual health screenings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> Efforts to find a <a href="/wiki/HIV_vaccine_development" title="HIV vaccine development">HIV vaccine</a> are ongoing whilst <a href="/wiki/Health_equity" title="Health equity">health inequities</a> have left certain population groups, like <a href="/wiki/Trans_woman" title="Trans woman">trans women</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> as well as resource limited regions, like <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, at greater risk of contracting HIV compared with, for example, <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>The outbreak of <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>, starting in 2019, and subsequent declaration of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> is a major pandemic event within the early 21st century. Causing global disruptions, millions of infections and deaths, the pandemic has caused suffering throughout communities. The pandemic has also seen some of the largest logistical organisations of <a href="/wiki/Goods" title="Goods">goods</a>, medical equipment, medical professionals, and military personnel since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> that highlights its far-reaching impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personalised_medicine">Personalised medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Personalised medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The rise of <a href="/wiki/Personalized_medicine" title="Personalized medicine">personalised medicine</a> in the 21st century has generated the possibility to develop diagnosis and treatments based on the individual characteristics of a person, rather than through generic practices that defined 20th century medicine. Areas like <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">DNA sequencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genetic_linkage" title="Genetic linkage">genetic mapping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gene_therapy" title="Gene therapy">gene therapy</a>, imaging protocols, <a href="/wiki/Proteomics" title="Proteomics">proteomics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stem-cell_therapy" title="Stem-cell therapy">stem cell therapy</a>, and wireless health monitoring devices<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> are all rising innovations that can help medical professionals fine tune treatment to the individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telemedicine">Telemedicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Telemedicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Remote_surgery" title="Remote surgery">Remote surgery</a> is another recent development, with the transatlantic <a href="/wiki/Lindbergh_operation" title="Lindbergh operation">Lindbergh operation</a> in 2001 as a groundbreaking example.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions_5">Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People_7">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes_in_medical_history">Themes in medical history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Themes in medical history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racism_in_medicine">Racism in medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Racism in medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">Racism</a> has a long history in how medicine has evolved and established itself, both in terms of racism experience upon patients, professionals, and wider systematic violence within medical institutions and systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> See: <a href="/wiki/Medical_racism_in_the_United_States" title="Medical racism in the United States">medical racism in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Race_and_health" title="Race and health">race and health</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scientific_racism" title="Scientific racism">scientific racism</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_medicine">Women in medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Women in medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_medicine" title="Women in medicine">Women in medicine</a></div>
<p>Women have always served as healers and midwives since ancient times. However, the professionalization of medicine forced them increasingly to the sidelines. As hospitals multiplied they relied in Europe on orders of Roman Catholic nun-nurses, and German Protestant and Anglican deaconesses in the early 19th century. They were trained in traditional methods of physical care that involved little knowledge of medicine.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-asylum_numbers-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-asylum_numbers_162-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
England and Wales had nine county and borough asylums in 1827 with an average capacity of a little over 100 patients, but by 1890 there were 66 such asylums containing on average 800 patients each;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> the total number of patients so confined increased from 1,027 in 1827 to 74,004 in 1900.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> Similarly, in Germany, between 1852 and 1898 the asylum population increased seven-fold from 11,622 to 74,087 patients during a period when the total population had only grown by ten per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otto_marx_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-otto_marx-158">[158]</a></sup> In America the asylum population had risen to almost 250,000 on the eve of the First World War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
